Miracles
intermediate
4 min
Christian Miracle Argument and Its Refutation
Razi answers the Christian miracle argument by attributing miracles to God's response to prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how classical Muslim theologians refuted the Christian argument that Jesus's miracles prove his divinity, by attributing them to God's response to prayer.

Core Idea
Miracles done at a prophet's prayer prove prophethood, not divinity.

In this passage, Imam al-Razi presents a core Christian argument for the divinity of Jesus based on his miracles, and then provides a concise refutation. Understanding this exchange clarifies an important distinction in Islamic theology: miracles are signs of prophethood, not evidence of divine incarnation. The argument hinges on the role of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the structure: first the Christian claim, then the answer.
2
Understand the Christian claim
The Christians argue that Jesus revived the dead and cured the blind/leprous. They say this requires divine power, implying Jesus had it.
This is a classic argument from miracles.
3
Analyze Razi's response
Razi does not deny the miracles but reinterprets their cause. He says God performed them in response to Jesus's prayer, as a sign of Jesus's prophethood.
Key phrase: على وفق دعائه (in response to his prayer).
4
Grasp the theological implication
The refutation preserves God's exclusive power while affirming Jesus as a miracle-working prophet. Miracles are signs, not proofs of divinity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحتج النصارى على قولهم : بأن عيسى أحيى الموتى، وأبرأ الأكمه والأبرص، وهذا لا يمكن إلا بالقدرة الإلهية.
والجواب : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : إنه تعالى هو الذي أحيى الموتى وأبرأ الأكمه والأبرص على وفق دعائه إظهارا لمعجزته؟
The Christians argued for their doctrine: that Jesus revived the dead, and cured the blind and leprous, and this cannot be except by divine power. The answer: Why is it not permissible to say that He (exalted) is the one who revived the dead and cured the blind and leprous in response to his prayer as a manifestation of his miracle?
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage presents the Christian argument from miracles and the Muslim response. The Christians claim that Jesus's miracles prove his divinity. The answer refutes that: God performed these miracles at Jesus's prayer as a miracle itself, not because Jesus had divine nature. Thus miracles do not prove incarnation.

Key Terms
إحياء الموتى (ihya al-mawta)
أبرأ الأكمه والأبرص (abraa al-akmah wal-abras)
معجزة (mu'jiza)
دعاء (du'a)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many people think that Christian miracles prove Jesus is God or part of a Trinity.
Correction: Islamic theology holds that all miracles are performed by God, and prophets may be granted miracles as signs, but that does not make them divine.

Checkpoint
According to al-Razi, how did Jesus perform miracles?
A) By his own divine power
B) By God's power in answer to his prayer
C) By inherited power
D) By magic

Key Takeaway
Miracles are signs of prophethood, not proof of divinity; they occur by God's power in response to a prophet's prayer.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness something miraculous, do you instinctively attribute it to the person's own power or to God's response to their faith? Which pattern does your heart lean toward, and how does this lesson recalibrate that instinct?
?
The Christians saw Jesus's miracles and concluded he was divine. What ‘miracles’ in your life—blessings, successes, or talents—have you mistakenly credited to yourself or others rather than to God? Will you consciously redirect that credit today?
?
This lesson hinges on the phrase 'in response to his prayer.' When was the last time you saw an answered prayer as a sign pointing not to the one who prayed, but to the One who answered? How can you make that perspective habitual?

Miracles
beginner
5 min
Razi's Argument from Moses' Miracle
Razi compares Moses' miracle to Jesus' to refute Christian arguments.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses an a fortiori argument comparing Moses' miracle to Jesus' miracles to refute the Christian doctrine of hulul (indwelling).

Core Idea
If Jesus' miracles prove divine indwelling, Moses' greater miracle must also—an absurd conclusion.

Razi continues his refutation of Christian doctrines by drawing a comparison between the miracles of Jesus and Moses. He argues that if Jesus' miracles are taken as proof of divine indwelling (hulul), then Moses' even more astonishing miracle would also imply indwelling, which Christians would reject. This reductio ad absurdum strengthens Razi's case.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its English translation carefully to understand the flow of Razi's argument.
2
Identify the comparison
Note that Razi compares Jesus reviving the dead to Moses turning a staff into a serpent. He claims Moses' miracle is 'more astonishing'.
3
Understand the a fortiori logic
Razi uses an a fortiori (even more so) argument: if lesser miracle (Jesus') indicates hulul, then greater miracle (Moses') should also indicate it.
This is a logical reductio ad absurdum.
4
Observe the conclusion
Razi concludes that the Christian and incarnationist doctrines are too base and low for a rational person to consider.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأيضًا كما ظهر إحياء الموتى على يدي عيسى فقد ظهر على يدي موسى لأنه قلب العصا ثعبانا ، بل هو أعجب؛ لأن انقلاب الخشبة ثعبانا عظيمًا أعجب من انقلاب الميت حيا ، فإن دلت معجزات عيسى على الحلول والاتحاد فبأن تدل معجزات موسى على هذا الحلول - وبالله التوفيق - أولى. وبالجملة : فمذهب النصارى والحلولية أخس وأذل من أن يلتفت العاقل إليه.
Also, just as the revival of the dead appeared at the hands of Jesus, it appeared at the hands of Moses because he turned the staff into a serpent—indeed it is more astonishing, because the transformation of wood into a great serpent is more astonishing than the transformation of the dead into living. So if Jesus's miracles indicate indwelling and union, then Moses' miracles should indicate this indwelling even more so. And in short, the doctrine of the Christians and the incarnationists is too base and low for a rational person to pay attention to it.
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage uses an a fortiori argument: if Jesus's miracles prove hulul, then Moses' greater miracle (staff to serpent) should also prove it, leading to an absurd conclusion that prophets like Moses also had divine indwelling. Since this is unacceptable, the Christian argument fails. The passage ends with a strong condemnation of these doctrines.

Key Terms
معجزة (mu'jiza)
عصا (asa)
ثعبان (thu'ban)
حلول (hulul)
اتحاد (ittihad)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Razi denies that Jesus performed miracles.
Correction: Razi does not deny Jesus' miracles; he accepts them but argues they do not prove hulul because Moses' even greater miracle would then also prove hulul, which Christians reject.

Checkpoint
According to al-Razi, which miracle is more astonishing?
A) Jesus reviving the dead
B) Moses turning the staff into a serpent
C) Both are equal
D) Neither

Key Takeaway
Razi uses the greater miracle of Moses to show that Christian claims of hulul lead to absurdity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you willing to follow a rational argument even when it challenges a belief you hold dear, or do you cling to what is comfortable?
?
When you hear of miracles, do you use them to justify your own biases, or do you seek the truth behind them as Razi does?

Miracles
beginner
4 min
Classification of Miracles: Sensory and Intellectual
Razi introduces the second premise and classifies miracles into sensory and intellectual types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Razi's twofold classification of the Prophet's miracles into sensory and intellectual types, and the three subdivisions of sensory miracles.

Core Idea
Miracles are either sensory (perceptible) or intellectual (rational); sensory miracles involve essence or attributes.

Razi provides a clear taxonomy of the Prophet's miracles beyond the Qur'an. He distinguishes between miracles that are perceptible by the senses and those that are grasped by the intellect. This classification helps organize the many reported miracles into a logical framework.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main types
Read the passage and note that Razi divides miracles into two types: sensory (hissiyya) and intellectual ('aqliyya). Understand the general distinction.
Sensory miracles are those that can be seen, heard, or felt; intellectual miracles are understood through reason.
2
Examine the three sensory categories
Focus on the three subdivisions of sensory miracles: matters external to his essence, matters in his essence, and matters in his attributes. Think of examples for each.
Examples: splitting the moon (external), the seal of prophethood (in essence), truthfulness (attribute).
3
Reflect on the role of intellectual miracles
Consider why Razi includes intellectual miracles as a separate category. The Qur'an itself is the prime example of an intellectual miracle that appeals to reason.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما المقدمة الثانية - وهي أن المعجزات ظهرت على وفق دعواه - فاعلم أن اعتماد المتكلمين في هذه المسألة على أن القرآن معجز والقرآن ظهر على وفق دعواه فيلزم من هاتين المقدمتين أن المعجزة ظهرت على وفق دعواه، وهذا دليل طويل، وفيه مباحث كثيرة، وقد استقصينا فيه الكلام في كتاب " نهاية العقول". واعلم أن الرسول الله كانت له معجزات كثيرة سوى القرآن والعلماء أفردوا في ذكرها كتباً. وضبط القول فيها : أن نقول : معجزاته قسمان: حسية وعقلية. أما الحسية فثلاثة أقسام: أحدها: أمور خارجة عن ذاته. وثانيها : أمور في ذاته وثالثها: أمور في صفاته.
As for the second premise—that miracles appeared in accordance with his claim—know that the reliance of the theologians on this issue is that the Qur'an is a miracle, and the Qur'an appeared in accordance with his claim, so from these two premises it follows that the miracle appeared in accordance with his claim. This is a long proof, and it contains many investigations, and we have exhausted the discussion of it in the book 'Nihayat al-'Uqul'. Know also that the Messenger of God had many miracles besides the Qur'an, and the scholars have written separate books mentioning them. The precise statement concerning them is that we say: his miracles are of two types: sensory and intellectual. As for the sensory, they are of three categories: first: matters external to his essence; second: matters in his essence; third: matters in his attributes.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage introduces the second premise of the proof for prophethood: that miracles appeared according to the Prophet's claim, and the main evidence is the Qur'an. It mentions that there is a long proof in another book. Then it clarifies that besides the Qur'an, the Prophet had many miracles. They are divided into two types: sensory (hissiyya) and intellectual ('aqliyya). Then it subdivides sensory miracles into three categories: those external to his essence (like splitting the moon), those in his essence (like the seal between his shoulders), and those in his attributes (like his truthfulness and courage). This classification sets the framework for the examples that follow.

Key Terms
معجزة (miracle)
حسية (sensory)
عقلية (intellectual)
ذات (essence)
صفات (attributes)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that intellectual miracles are not real miracles because they are not physically perceptible.
Correction: Razi explicitly includes intellectual miracles as a valid type. The Qur'an itself is an intellectual miracle, as its inimitability is proven through reason.

Checkpoint
How many categories of sensory miracles does Imam Razi enumerate?
A) Two
B) Three
C) Four
D) Five

Key Takeaway
Razi classifies the Prophet's miracles into sensory (with three subtypes) and intellectual, providing a comprehensive framework.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of the three categories of sensory miracles—external to his essence, in his essence, or in his attributes—do you find most personally compelling for strengthening your own faith in the Prophet? Why?
?
The Quran is considered an intellectual miracle. When you read the Quran, do you approach it as a rational proof? How does that perspective change the way you engage with its verses?
?
Razi lists the Prophet's many miracles besides the Quran. How often do you reflect on the diversity of proofs for his prophethood? What is one specific miracle (besides the Quran) that you can study and internalize this week to deepen your certainty?

Miracles
beginner
5 min
External Sensory Miracles of the Prophet
Razi lists examples of sensory miracles external to the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the category of external sensory miracles and be able to list several examples from the life of the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Core Idea
External miracles are tangible signs of prophethood witnessed by others.

In this passage, Imam al-Razi presents the first category of sensory miracles: those that occurred outside the Prophet's own person. These are public, visible events that serve as clear proofs of his prophethood. Let's explore these remarkable occurrences.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without analyzing. Let the list of miracles sink in.
2
Identify the category
Notice that this is the first category: miracles external to the Prophet's essence. All examples are events that happened around him.
3
Reflect on the diversity
The miracles involve inanimate objects (moon, tree, stone), living things (she-camel, sheep), and food/water. This shows the breadth of prophetic miracles.
4
Consider the transmission
These miracles are mutawatir (widely transmitted), making them reliable proofs. Reflect on how they strengthen belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما القسم الأول : - وهو الأشياء الخارجة عن ذاته - فهو كانشقاق القمر، واجتذاب الشجر، وتسليم الحجر عليه ونبوع الماء من بين أصابعه، وإشباع الخلق الكثير من الطعام القليل وحنين الخشب وشكاية الناقة وشهادة الشاة المسمومة، وإظلال السحاب قبل مبعثه وما كان من حال أبي جهل وصخرته حين اراد ان يضربها على رأسه وما كان من شاة أم معبد حين مسح يده على ضرعها.
As for the first category—which is the things external to his essence—it includes the splitting of the moon, the drawing of the tree, the greeting of the stone to him, the gushing of water from between his fingers, the satisfying of a large multitude with little food, the moaning of the wood, the complaint of the she-camel, the testimony of the poisoned sheep, the cloud casting shade before his mission, and the incident of Abu Jahl and his rock when he wanted to strike it on his head, and the incident of the sheep of Umm Ma'bad when he wiped his hand on its udder.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage lists the first category of sensory miracles: those external to the Prophet's essence. It enumerates a series of well-known miracles: the splitting of the moon, the tree being drawn to him, the stone greeting him, water flowing from his fingers, feeding a large crowd with little food, the wood moaning, the she-camel complaining, the poisoned sheep speaking, the cloud shading him before his mission, the protection from Abu Jahl's rock, and the miracle of Umm Ma'bad's sheep. Each of these is a concrete event witnessed by people.

Key Terms
انشقاق القمر (splitting of the moon)
نبوع الماء (gushing of water)
حنين الخشب (moaning of wood)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think these stories are mythical legends without historical basis.
Correction: In kalam, these miracles are accepted as mutawatir (mass-transmitted) and thus constitute certain knowledge.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT mentioned as an external sensory miracle in this passage?
A) Splitting of the moon
B) Water gushing from fingers
C) The Isra and Mi'raj (Night Journey)
D) The greeting of the stone

Key Takeaway
External sensory miracles are tangible events that provide clear evidence of prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of these miracles strikes you as most powerful, and why? Does your heart respond with awe, or have you become desensitized to the miraculous?
?
The Prophet ﷺ was given these tangible signs—if you had witnessed one, would it have transformed your faith? What is stopping you from having that same certainty now?
?
Umm Ma'bad's sheep gave milk after a touch; the wood moaned in longing. These external miracles call for a response. Will you content yourself with merely knowing them, or will you let them deepen your conviction and draw you closer to the One who sent them?

Miracles
beginner
4 min
Sensory Miracles in the Prophet's Essence
Razi lists sensory miracles that occurred in the Prophet's own person.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three sensory miracles that occurred in the Prophet's own person as listed by Imam Razi.

Core Idea
Three miraculous signs adorned the Prophet's very being: light, seal, and form.

Imam Razi continues his classification of miracles by turning to those that are intrinsic to the Prophet's person. These are not external events but qualities of his own body and lineage. In this passage, he lists three such miracles: the transmitted light, the seal of prophethood, and his physiognomic appearance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the three elements Razi lists: the light, the seal, and the appearance.
2
Analyze the light of prophethood
Understand that the light refers to a luminous sign passed through generations, culminating in the Prophet. This is a miracle of lineage.
3
Examine the seal between his shoulders
This physical mark is well-attested in hadith. It was a tangible sign for those who saw him.
4
Explore physiognomy as evidence
Razi appeals to the science of firasa, which reads character from appearance. The Prophet's form itself testified to his truth.
5
Reflect on the category
These are miracles inherent in his essence, not external events. They show that his prophethood was written in his very being.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثاني : - وهو الأحوال العائدة إلى ذاته فهو مثل النور الذي كان ينتقل من أب على أب إلى أن خرج إلى الدنيا وما كان من الخاتم بين كتفيه، وما من خلقته وصورته التي هي بحكم الفراسة دالة على نبوته.
As for the second category—which is the conditions pertaining to his essence—it includes the light that was transmitted from father to father until it came into the world, and the seal between his shoulders, and the qualities of his form and appearance which, by the rule of physiognomy (firasa), indicate his prophethood.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage lists the second category of sensory miracles: those in the Prophet's essence. It mentions three things: the light that was passed from one ancestor to another until it reached the Prophet (the light of prophethood), the seal of prophethood between his shoulders, and his physical form and appearance which, through the science of physiognomy, indicated his prophethood. These are miracles inherent in his person.

Key Terms
نور (light)
خاتم النبوة (seal of prophethood)
فراسة (physiognomy)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What are the three things mentioned as miracles in the Prophet's essence?
A) The light, the seal, and his appearance
B) The light, the splitting of the moon, and the seal
C) The seal, the rock of Abu Jahl, and the light
D) The light, his truthfulness, and the seal

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's very nature contained miraculous signs—his lineage, his seal, and his form—that testified to his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The light of prophethood passed through generations to reach the Prophet ﷺ. What spiritual legacy are you carrying forward to the next generation? Are you actively transmitting it, or are you a dead link in the chain?
?
If the Prophet's very appearance testified to his truthfulness, how much weight do you give to external signs of sincerity when you judge others? How often do you ignore the inner light in favor of superficial judgments?
?
The seal between his shoulders was a physical reminder of his mission. What physical signs in your life remind you daily of your purpose and accountability to Allah? If none exist, what needs to change today?

Miracles
beginner
6 min
Sensory Miracles in the Prophet's Attributes
Razi lists sensory miracles in the Prophet's attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand four miraculous attributes of the Prophet Muhammad that serve as sensory proofs of his prophethood.

Core Idea
The Prophet's perfect attributes are not just virtues—they are miracles.

Imam Razi continues his discussion of sensory miracles by turning to the Prophet's own attributes. He enumerates four qualities that, in their perfection and consistency, go beyond ordinary human capacity. These attributes—truthfulness, sinlessness, courage, and compassion—are witnessed by those who interacted with him and serve as clear signs of his prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic text once without translation. Notice the four attributes Razi lists and how each is introduced with a number.
The passage begins with 'وأما القسم الثالث' indicating this is the third category of miracles.
2
Identify the four attributes
Razi lists four attributes: truthfulness (صدق), sinlessness (عصمة), courage (شجاعة), and compassion (شفقة). For each, note the evidence he provides.
The evidence includes both rational argument (e.g., enemies would have exposed lies) and Quranic quotes.
3
Understand why these are miraculous
Reflect on why these attributes are considered sensory miracles. They are not merely moral virtues but extraordinary in their consistency and perfection, beyond normal human capacity.
The commentary clarifies this distinction.
4
Connect to the overall argument
These attributes are part of Razi's broader proof of prophethood. Consider how they complement the earlier categories of miracles.
This lesson stands alone but also builds on previous lessons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثالث : - وهو ما يتعلق بصفاته - وهي كثيرة، ونحن نشير إلى بعضها : هذا فالأول: أن أحدًا ما سمع في مهمات الدين ولا في مهمات الدنيا كذبًا البتة، فلو صدر عنه الكذب مرة واحدة لاجتهد أعداؤه في تشهيره وإظهاره. والثاني : أنه ما أقدم على فعل قبيح لا قبل النبوة ولا بعدها. الثالث : أنه لم يفر عن أحد من أعدائه لا قبل النبوة ولا بعدها - وإن عظم الخوف - مثل يوم الأحزاب، وهذا يدل على أنه كان قوي القلب بمواعيد الله، حيث قال: ﴿ وَاللهُ يَعْصِمُكَ مِنَ النَّاسِ ﴾ [المائدة : ٦٧] وقال: ﴿حَسْبَكَ الله﴾ [الأنفال : ٦٢] وقال: ﴿إِلَّا نَصُرُوهُ فَقَدْ نَصَرَهُ اللهُ ﴾ [التوبة : ٤٠] . الرابع : أنه كان عظيم الشفقة والرحمة على أمته وقال الله تعالى: ﴿فَلَا نَذْهَبْ نَفْسُكَ عَلَيْهِمْ حَسَرَاتٍ ﴾ [فَاطِر : ۸] وقال تعالى: ﴿فَلَعَلَّكَ بَخِعٌ نَفْسَكَ﴾ [الكهف: ٦] وقال : عليهم الج [الحجر: ۸۸] وقال : وعزيز عليه ما عنتم حريص عليكم
As for the third category—which pertains to his attributes—they are many, and we point to some of them: This: first: that no one ever heard from him a single lie in matters of religion or worldly matters; if he had lied once, his enemies would have striven to publicize and spread it. Second: that he never committed a reprehensible act either before prophethood or after it. Third: that he never fled from any enemy either before prophethood or after it—even in great fear—like the day of the Confederates (Ahzab), and this indicates that he was strong-hearted due to the promises of God, where He said: 'And God will protect you from the people' (Quran 5:67), and He said: 'God is sufficient for you' (Quran 8:62), and He said: 'If you do not help him, God has already helped him' (Quran 9:40). Fourth: that he was immense in compassion and mercy towards his nation, and God Almighty said: 'So do not let your soul go out in grief over them' (Quran 35:8), and He said: 'Perhaps you will kill yourself with grief' (Quran 18:6), and He said: ... [unclear] (Quran 15:88), and He said: 'He is concerned over your suffering, eager for your [good]' (Quran 9:128).
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage lists the third category of sensory miracles: those pertaining to the Prophet's attributes. It enumerates four attributes that are miraculous. First, his complete truthfulness: he never lied, and if he had, his enemies would have exposed him. Second, his sinlessness ('isma): he never committed a bad deed before or after prophethood. Third, his courage: he never fled from any enemy, even in the most fearful situations like the Battle of the Trench (Ahzab), which proves his reliance on God's promises. Fourth, his immense compassion and mercy towards his community, as evidenced by Quranic verses urging him not to grieve excessively for them. These attributes are miraculous because they are beyond normal human capacity.

Key Terms
صدق
عصمة
شجاعة
شفقة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These attributes are merely moral virtues, not miracles.
Correction: In kalam, the consistency and perfection of these attributes beyond normal human capacity make them sensory miracles.

Checkpoint
Which attribute is NOT listed in the third category of sensory miracles?
A) Truthfulness
B) Sinlessness
C) Generosity
D) Courage

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's truthfulness, sinlessness, courage, and compassion are sensory miracles that serve as proofs of his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you told a lie, even a small 'white lie'? How does the Prophet's complete truthfulness expose your own failure? What practical step will you take this week to be more truthful?
?
Do you flee from difficult situations because of fear of people? What divine promise from the Quran—like 'God is sufficient for you'—can you hold onto today to face your fear instead of running?
?
Are you truly compassionate to those around you, or do you overlook their struggles? How does the Prophet's overwhelming mercy for his nation (even those who hurt him) challenge your heart? Will you perform one concrete act of compassion today?

Miracles
intermediate
8 min
Rational Miracles: The Prophet's Answered Supplications
Razi enumerates six answered-supplication miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi uses six specific answered prayers as rational proofs of the Prophet's prophethood.

Core Idea
Answered supplications are tangible evidence of divine backing.

Razi presents a series of historical events where the Prophet's prayers were answered in unmistakable ways. Each of these six examples forms a logical demonstration that his prophethood was supported by Allah. This lesson explores these proofs and their significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
The passage is a list of six distinct examples; notice the flow.
2
Identify the six examples
Go through each example and note the specific miracle: drought, tearing of kingdom, lion, knowledge for Ibn Abbas, invisibility at cave, sinking horse.
Each example has a clear cause (prayer) and effect (answer).
3
Understand the logical proof
Ask yourself: How does each example demonstrate that the Prophet's prayer was answered? Why does this count as a rational miracle? Razi uses these as evidence of prophethood.
These are not just stories; they are rationally presented arguments.
4
Reflect on the cumulative evidence
Consider how the multiple examples strengthen the overall argument. Each one is a separate proof, but together they build a strong case.
The variety of situations increases credibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الثلاثون : النوع الرابع في معجزاته العقلية أنه - عليه الصلاة والسلام - كان مجاب الدعوة، ويدل عليه وجوه : أحدها: أن قريشًا لما بالغوا في إيذائه دعا عليهم فقال: «اللهم اشدد وطأنك على مضر، واجعلها عليهم سنين كسني يوسف والله تعالى منع من إنزال المطر عليهم، فبطلت زراعاتهم وهلكت مواشيهم واستولى القحط عليهم، فجاؤوا يشفعون إليه حتى يسأل الله تعالى إنزال المطر عليهم، فلما سأل ذلك جاءهم المطر حتى خافوا الغرق فعادوا وسألوه أن يدعوا الله حتى ينزل المطر بقدر الحاجة، فقال: اللهم حوالينا ولا علينا، اللهم على الجبال وبطون الأودية» فاندفع ذلك البلاء عنهم. وثانيها : أنه لما كتب إلى كسرى - ملك العجم - كتابا ومزق الملك كتابه وبعث إليه حفنة من تراب بلدته قال : اللهم مزق ملكه ثم قال للصحابة - رضوان الله عليهم أجمعين : إنه بعث تراب بلدته إلينا وهذا على أنا نملك بلاده فكان الأمر كما قال. وثالثها : أنه له قال في حق عتبة بن أبي لهب : اللهم سلط عليه كلبا من كلابك فافترسه الأسد. ورابعها : أنه دعا لابن عمه عبد الله بن عباس فقال : «اللهم فقهه في الدين وعلمه التأويل فصار ابن عباس ببركة هذا الدعاء خير المفسرين. وخامسها أن الكفار لما وصلوا إلى الغار قرأ هو الله عليهم : وَجَعَلْنَا مِنْ بَيْنِ أَيْدِيهِمْ سَدًّا وَمِنْ خَلْفِهِمْ سَدًّا [يس: ٩] فأولئك الكفار كانوا ينظرون إلى الغار وما كانوا يرون النبي . وسادسها : أنه لما خرج من الغار ذهب خلفه جمع من الكفار، فلما قرب واحد منهم قال : يا أرض خذيه فغاصت قوائم فرس ذلك الكافر في الأرض ببركة دعائه.
The thirtieth question: The fourth type concerning his rational miracles, namely that he – peace be upon him – was one whose supplication was answered. This is indicated by several aspects: First: That when Quraysh went to extremes in harming him, he supplicated against them saying: 'O Allah, make your punishment severe on Mudar, and make it for them years like the years of Joseph.' And Allah prevented rain from falling on them, so their crops failed, their livestock perished, and drought overcame them. So they came interceding with him until he asked Allah to send down rain. When he asked that, rain came to them until they feared drowning, so they returned and asked him to supplicate to Allah to send rain in the needed amount. So he said: 'O Allah, around us and not upon us. O Allah, on the mountains and in the valleys.' So that calamity was repelled from them. Second: That when he wrote to Chosroes, the king of Persia, and the king tore up his letter and sent him a handful of soil from his town, he said: 'O Allah, tear up his kingdom.' Then he said to the Companions – may Allah be pleased with them all – 'He sent us the soil of his town, and this indicates that we will possess his lands.' And it happened as he said. Third: That when he said regarding 'Utba ibn Abi Lahab: 'O Allah, set upon him one of Your dogs,' and a lion devoured him. Fourth: That he supplicated for his cousin 'Abdullah ibn 'Abbas saying: 'O Allah, make him learned in religion and teach him interpretation,' and Ibn 'Abbas became the best of commentators by the blessing of this supplication. Fifth: That when the disbelievers reached the cave, he recited to them: 'And We placed before them a barrier and behind them a barrier' (Ya Sin 36:9), and those disbelievers were looking at the cave but did not see the Prophet. Sixth: That when he came out of the cave, a group of disbelievers followed him. When one of them approached, he said: 'O earth, take him!' So the legs of the horse of that disbeliever sank into the earth by the blessing of his supplication.
Source pages p. 304

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth type of proof: rational miracles (al-mu'jizat al-'aqliyya), specifically the Prophet's answered supplications (ijabat al-da'wa). It enumerates six examples: (1) The prayer for drought against Quraysh followed by rain when he interceded; (2) The prayer against Chosroes that his kingdom be torn up, with the interpretation of the handful of soil; (3) The prayer that a lion devour 'Utba ibn Abi Lahab; (4) The prayer for Ibn 'Abbas to gain deep religious knowledge, which was fulfilled; (5) The recitation of a verse at the cave causing invisibility; (6) The prayer causing a horse to sink into the earth. Each example demonstrates that Allah answered the Prophet's call, confirming his prophethood.

Key Terms
المعجزات العقلية
مجاب الدعوة
إجابة الدعوة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These events are just historical anecdotes without evidential value.
Correction: Razi presents them as rational proofs: each event shows a specific prayer followed by a precise outcome, which cannot be coincidental and thus confirms divine backing.

Checkpoint
Which miracle is associated with 'Abdullah ibn 'Abbas in the fourth type?
A) The rain prayer
B) The lion devouring an enemy
C) The prayer for religious knowledge
D) The sinking of a horse

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's answered supplications serve as rational miracles that confirm his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet's supplication for Ibn 'Abbas was specific: 'Teach him the interpretation (of the Quran).' Do you have a clear, specific request for Allah regarding your own religious knowledge? What exactly are you asking for, and what step will you take today to pursue it?
?
When the Prophet prayed against his enemies, the result was immediate and exact. When you feel wronged, do you trust that Allah's justice is more precise than your desire for revenge? What would it mean for you to leave the outcome entirely to Allah, as the Prophet did?
?
The Prophet's supplications were answered because he was the beloved of Allah. Look at your own supplications: do you pray with the certainty that Allah hears and will respond? If not, what is holding you back from that level of trust, and how can you build it starting today?

Miracles

Classification of Unseen Prophecies
Classification of prophecies into past and future, with four examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam Razi classifies the Prophet's prophecies of the unseen into past and future categories, and you will examine four Quranic examples of fulfilled future prophecies.

Core Idea
Prophetic knowledge of the unseen, both past and future, is a powerful proof of prophethood.

Imam Razi continues his discussion of miracles by focusing on the Prophet's reports of the unseen. He first distinguishes between knowledge of past events and future events, then provides concrete examples from the Quran that were later fulfilled. The first few examples demonstrate how specific predictions about battles and conquests came true exactly as foretold.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening classification
Begin by reading the first two sentences that divide prophecies into past and future. Notice how the author argues that informing of past events without a teacher or book is itself miraculous.
2
Identify the four examples
Read the first four examples (defeat at Badr, promise of one of two parties, Bedouins called to fight, defeat of Romans). Observe that each prophecy was given before the event and was fulfilled.
The fourth example about the Romans is significant because it was fulfilled in stages.
3
Reflect on the miraculous nature
Ask yourself: could any human have predicted these specific future events with such accuracy? The author's point is that only divine revelation could produce such precise foreknowledge.
This connects to the broader proof of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع السادس من معجزاته : إخباره عن الغيوب
أما إخباره عن المغيبات الماضية فهو أنه أخبر عن وقائع المتقدمين من غير قراءة كتاب ولا استفادة من إنسان.
وأما إخباره عن الغيوب المستقبلة فهو على قسمين : منه ما ورد في القرآن ومنه ما ورد في الأخبار.
أما الذي ورد في القرآن فكثير :
أحدها : قوله تعالى : سَيَهْزَمُ الْجَمْعُ وَيُوَلُّونَ الدُّبُرَ [القمر: ٤٥] والسين في قوله ما حرم الله للاستقبال، والسورة مكية، ثم إنه حصل ذلك يوم بدر.
وثانيها : قوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذْ يَعِدُكُمُ اللهُ إِحْدَى الطَّائِفَتَيْنِ أَنَّهَا لَكُمْ﴾ [الأنفال: ٧] وقد كانت لهم.
وثالثها: قوله تعالى: ﴿قُل لِّلْمُخَلَّفِينَ مِنَ الْأَعْرَابِ سَتُدْعَوْنَ إِلَى قَوْمٍ أُولِي بَأْسٍ شَدِيدٍ﴾ [الفتح: ١٦] وقد وقع ذلك؛ لأن المراد من القوم أولي البأس عند بعضهم بنو حنيفة، وقد دعا أبو بكر [؟] إلى قتالهم، وعند آخرين هم فارس، وقد دعا عمر بن الخطاب [؟] إلى قتالهم.
ورابعها قوله تعالى : غُلِبَتِ الرُّومُ [الروم: ٢-٣] وكان كما أخبر.
وخامسها : قوله تعالى: ﴿سَنُرِيهِمْ آيَاتِنَا فِي الْآفَاقِ وَفِي أَنفُسِهِمْ﴾ [فصلت: ٥٣] ولا يمكن حمل الآية على الآيات الدالة على التوحيد ؛ لأنها كانت حاضرة، وقوله : سَنُرِيهِمْ للاستقبال، فلا بد أن يكون المراد منه فتح القرى المحيطة بـ مكة وبقوله : وفي أنفسهم فتح مكة وقد وقع.
وسادسها: قوله تعالى : ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِي فَرَضَ عَلَيْكَ الْقُرْآنَ لَرَادُّكَ إِلَى مَعَادٍ﴾ [القصص: ٨٥] أي إلى مكة وقد رده الله تعالى إليها.
وسابعها قوله : لِيُظْهِرَهُ عَلَى الدِّينِ كُلِّهِ [التوبة: ٣٣] وقد أظهره.
وثامنها قوله تعالى: ﴿وَعَدَ اللَّهُ الَّذِينَ آمَنُوا مِنكُمْ وَعَمِلُوا الصَّالِحَاتِ لَيَسْتَخْلِفَنَّهُمْ فِي﴾ [النور: ٥٥]
The sixth type of his miracles: his informing of the unseen. As for his informing of past hidden things, it is that he informed of the events of the ancients without reading a book or learning from a human. As for his informing of future hidden things, it is of two types: some occur in the Qur'an and some occur in the reports. As for what occurs in the Qur'an, it is abundant: First: His saying, exalted: 'The army will be defeated and they will turn their backs' [al-Qamar 45]. The 's' in His statement indicates future tense, and the sura is Meccan; then that happened on the day of Badr. Second: His saying, exalted: 'And when Allah promised you one of the two parties that it would be yours' [al-Anfal 7], and it was theirs. Third: His saying, exalted: 'Say to those who remained behind of the Bedouins, you will be called to a people of severe might' [al-Fath 16]; and that occurred, for the meaning of 'the people of severe might' according to some was Banu Hanifa, and Abu Bakr [?] summoned to fight them, and according to others they were Persia, and Umar ibn al-Khattab [?] summoned to fight them. Fourth: His saying, exalted: 'The Romans have been defeated' [al-Rum 2-3], and it was as he informed. Fifth: His saying, exalted: 'We will show them Our signs in the horizons and in themselves' [Fussilat 53]; and it is not possible to interpret the verse as the signs indicating tawhid because they were present, and His saying 'We will show them' is for future tense, so the intended meaning must be the conquest of the towns surrounding Mecca, and by 'And in themselves' the conquest of Mecca; and that occurred. Sixth: His saying, exalted: 'Indeed, the One who imposed the Qur'an upon you will return you to a place of return' [al-Qasas 85] i.e. to Mecca, and Allah returned him to it. Seventh: His saying: 'To make it prevail over all religion' [al-Tawba 33], and He made it prevail. Eighth: His saying, exalted: 'Allah has promised those who have believed among you and done righteous deeds that He will surely grant them succession in...' [al-Nur 55]
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is a classification and proof of the Prophet's miracles through his foretelling of the unseen (ikhbar an al-ghuyub). The author first divides the prophet's reports of the unseen into two categories: past events and future events. For past events, the argument is that the Prophet recounted histories of earlier nations without having learned them from books or teachers—this itself is miraculous. For future events, the author further divides into those reported in the Qur'an and those reported in the hadith. He then lists eight Qur'anic examples, following the order of the surahs. Each example is a specific prediction that was fulfilled exactly as stated: (1) the defeat of the Quraysh at Badr, foretold in a Meccan sura. (2) The promise that one of the two parties (the caravan or the army) would be theirs, which came true. (3) The prophecy that the Bedouins would be called to fight a people of severe might, interpreted as Banu Hanifa or Persia, which occurred under Abu Bakr and Umar. (4) The defeat of the Romans by the Persians, then later the Romans' victory as per the context. (5) The showing of signs in the horizons (conquests) and in themselves (conquest of Mecca). (6) The promise that the Prophet would return to Mecca, which happened in the conquest. (7) The dominance of Islam over all religions. (8) The promise of succession for the believers, cut off but clearly referring to the caliphate. The author's argument is that these predictions could not be from human knowledge, so they prove prophethood.

Key Terms
إخبار عن الغيوب
مغيبات
السين للاستقبال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Prophet's knowledge of past events could have been learned from earlier scriptures or teachers.
Correction: The author emphasizes he had no book or teacher, making his accurate recounting of ancient events a miracle.

Checkpoint
What is the main division of the Prophet's prophecies of the unseen according to this passage?
A) Past prophecies and future prophecies
B) Meccan and Medinan prophecies
C) Quranic and Hadith prophecies
D) Military and civil prophecies

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's knowledge of past and future unseen events, given without human learning, is a clear proof of his prophethood.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read about the Prophet's precise knowledge of future events like the defeat at Badr, do you feel a sense of assurance that your own future is in the hands of the One who revealed these prophecies? How does that impact your worries about tomorrow?
?
The Prophet knew the histories of past nations without reading any book. Are you truly convinced that he was a messenger from Allah, or do you still harbor doubts? What is one specific area in your life where you need to act on this conviction today?
?
If you had lived at the time of the Prophet and heard the prophecy of the Roman defeat, would you have believed it before it happened? What does that say about the strength of your current faith in the unseen promises of Allah in your own life?

Further Quranic Prophecies of the Future
Listing four more Quranic prophecies of future unseen events.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will study four more Quranic prophecies that were fulfilled exactly as foretold, strengthening the argument that the Prophet's knowledge of the future was miraculous.

Core Idea
Every Quranic prophecy about the future came true, proving divine origin.

Imam Razi continues listing Quranic prophecies of future unseen events. Each example is a specific prediction that was historically fulfilled, from the conquest of Mecca to the dominance of Islam. These examples reinforce that the Prophet could not have known such details by human means.

Guided Path
1
Read the remaining four examples
Focus on the fifth through eighth examples: signs in horizons and selves, return to Mecca, prevail over religion, and succession for believers. Notice how each uses a future tense verb (sīn or saufa).
2
Analyze the argument
For each example, the author notes the prophecy and its fulfillment. Reflect on how improbable it would be for a human to predict these exact events decades in advance.
3
Consider the cumulative evidence
Think about the combined effect of multiple fulfilled prophecies. This makes the case for prophethood even stronger than a single miracle.
The author implies that such consistency cannot be coincidence.

Source Text

Seventh: His saying: 'To make it prevail over all religion' [al-Tawba 33], and He made it prevail. Eighth: His saying, exalted: 'Allah has promised those who have believed among you and done righteous deeds that He will surely grant them succession in...' [al-Nur 55]

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the prophecies in the Quran were vague or could be interpreted in multiple ways after the fact.
Correction: The author shows that these prophecies were specific and used future tense, and their fulfillment was precise and undeniable.

Checkpoint
Which Quranic prophecy did the author interpret as referring to the conquest of Mecca?
A) 'The army will be defeated'
B) 'We will show them Our signs in the horizons and in themselves'
C) 'Indeed, the One who imposed the Qur'an upon you will return you to a place of return'
D) 'To make it prevail over all religion'

Key Takeaway
The fulfillment of these four specific Quranic prophecies, each using future tense, provides strong evidence that the Quran is from Allah and the Prophet is truthful.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
The same Quran that predicted the conquest of Mecca also commands you to pray, give charity, and fear Allah. How does the fulfillment of these prophecies affect your commitment to obeying those commands today?

Three Miracles of the Prophet
Al-Razi lists three specific miracles of the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three specific miracles that al-Razi uses as evidence for the Prophet's truthfulness.

Core Idea
Three distinct miracles confirm the Prophet's message.

Al-Razi now presents three concrete miracles as proofs of prophethood. Each miracle serves as a sign that the Prophet's claims were true. This lesson examines these three events and their significance as evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully to get a sense of the three miracles listed.
Notice that al-Razi frames them as the eighth, ninth, and tenth miracles in his list.
2
Identify each miracle
Identify the three miracles: the caliphate prophecy, the Night of Isra', and the revelation of hidden knowledge to al-Abbas.
Each miracle involves a different type of evidence: future prediction, unseen knowledge, and personal hidden details.
3
Reflect on the purpose
Consider why these events are considered miracles and how they serve as proofs of prophethood.
Al-Razi concludes that the Prophet's miracles are many, but these suffice as examples.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وثامنها : قوله : «الخلافة بعدي ثلاثون سنة وكانت خلافة الخلفاء الراشدين هذا القدر. و تاسعها : ليلة الإسراء فإنه أخبر قريشًا عن أمور فكانت كما أخبر. وعاشرها : قوله للعباس حين أسره : افد نفسك وابني أخيك عقيل بن أبي طالب ونوفل ابن الحارث، فإنك ذو مال فقال : لا مال عندي، فقال: «أين المال الذي وضعته بمكة عند أم الفضل وليس معكما أحد فقلت : إن أصبت في سفري فللفضل كذا ولعبد الله كذا ولفلان كذا ؟ فقال العباس : والذي بعثك بالحق نبيا ما علم هذا أحد غيري وإنك لرسول الله، وأسلم هو وعقيل. واعلم أن معجزات النبي كثيرة، واكتفينا ههنا بهذا القدر.
And the eighth of them: His statement: 'The caliphate after me is thirty years,' and the caliphate of the Rightly Guided Caliphs was this amount. And the ninth of them: The Night of Isra', for he informed Quraysh about matters, and they were as he informed. And the tenth of them: His statement to al-Abbas when he captured him: 'Ransom yourself, and the sons of my brother Aqil ibn Abi Talib and Nawfal ibn al-Harith, for you are wealthy.' He said: 'I have no wealth.' He said: 'Where is the wealth you placed in Mecca with Umm al-Fadl when no one was with you, and you said: If I am killed on my journey, then for al-Fadl such and such, and for Abdullah such and such, and for so-and-so such and such?' So al-Abbas said: 'By the One Who sent you with the truth as a prophet, no one knew this except me, and indeed you are the Messenger of Allah.' And he and Aqil embraced Islam. And know that the miracles of the Prophet are many, and we have sufficed here with this amount.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage enumerates three specific miracles of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) as evidence of his prophethood. The eighth miracle is the prophecy that the caliphate after him would last thirty years, which occurred as predicted. The ninth miracle is the Night of Isra' (the Ascension), where he accurately described events in Jerusalem to the Quraysh, confirming his truthfulness. The tenth miracle involves revealing hidden knowledge to al-Abbas about money he had secretly left with his wife, which led to al-Abbas and his nephew Aqil embracing Islam. The author concludes by noting that the Prophet's miracles are numerous, and he has only listed a sufficient sample.

الخلافة (caliphate)
الإسراء (the Night Journey)
العباس (al-Abbas)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These three are the only miracles of the Prophet.
Correction: Al-Razi explicitly states that the Prophet's miracles are many, and he has only listed a sufficient sample.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi presents three specific miracles—a fulfilled prophecy, the Night of Isra', and hidden knowledge—as evidence for the Prophet's prophethood, while noting that many more exist.

Proof of the Third Premise: Miracle as Divine Verification
Al-Razi proves that a miracle following a claim proves truthfulness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Razi uses logical reasoning and analogy to prove that a miracle following a claim of prophethood confirms the claimant's truthfulness.

Core Idea
A miracle is God's seal of approval on a prophet's claim.

In this passage, al-Razi continues his systematic proof of prophethood by establishing the third and final premise: that anyone who claims prophethood and is supported by a miracle must be truthful. He argues that a miracle, being beyond human power, is an act of Allah, and Allah would not support a liar. He illustrates this with a powerful analogy of a king verifying his messenger, then applies it to the miracle of the splitting of the moon to confirm the truthfulness of Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him).

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice how al-Razi builds his argument from general premise to specific example.
2
Identify the logical structure
The passage presents a premise, a logical indication, an analogy, and an application. Identify each part and see how they connect to prove the claim.
The key link is that a miracle is an act of Allah, and Allah's act of verification implies truthfulness.
3
Examine the analogy
Al-Razi uses the analogy of a king and a messenger. Understand how the analogy works: the king's extraordinary act serves as verification of the messenger's claim. Then see how this applies to Allah and the Prophet.
The analogy highlights the principle of 'necessary knowledge' – observers directly perceive the verification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وثبت بمجموع ما ذكرنا أنه ادعى الرسالة وظهرت المعجزة على وفق دعواه. وأما المقدمة الثالثة - وهي أن كل من كان كذلك كان صادقًا - فالذي يدل عليه : هو أن المعجزات لما عجز عنها كان ذلك فعلا من أفعال الله تعالى خلقه في هذه عقيب دعواه، وخلق المعجزة عقيب الدعوى، يدل على تصديق مدعي الرسالة. ومثاله : أنه إذا جلس الملك العظيم على سرير مملكته فقام واحد وقال: إني رسول هذا الملك إلى أهل مملكته ثم قال يا أيها الملك إن كنت صادقًا الدعوى فافعل شيئًا يحالف عاداتك، فإذا فعل ذلك الملك في تلك الساعة فعلا يخالف عادته علم الحاضرون بالضرورة أنه إنما فعل ذلك لأجل تصديق ذلك المدعى، فهكذا ههنا أن محمدا صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : يا أيها الناس إني رسول الله إليكم، ثم قال : يا إلهي إن كنت صادقًا في هذه الدعوى فاجعل القمر منشقا بنصفين، فإذا انشق القمر علم كل واحد بالضرورة أنه تعالى إنما شقه بنصفين لأجل تصديقه، فثبت أن خلق المعجزة على وفق الدعوى تصديق من الله لذلك المدعى، وكل من صدقه الله تعالى فهو صادق.
And it is established by all that we have mentioned that he claimed prophethood and a miracle appeared in accordance with his claim. As for the third premise—that everyone who is like this is truthful—what indicates it is that since miracles are beyond human capacity, that is an act of Allah, may He be exalted, which He created at this moment following his claim, and the creation of the miracle subsequent to the claim indicates the verification of the claimant of prophethood. An example: if a great king sits on the throne of his kingdom, and a person stands and says: 'I am the messenger of this king to the people of his kingdom,' then says: 'O king, if I am truthful in my claim, do something contrary to your customs,' and if the king at that moment does an act contrary to his custom, the attendees necessarily know that he only did that to verify that claimant. Thus here, Muhammad (peace be upon him) said: 'O people, I am the Messenger of Allah to you,' then said: 'O my God, if I am truthful in this claim, split the moon into two halves.' So when the moon split, everyone necessarily knew that He, exalted, only split it into two halves to verify him. So it is established that the creation of a miracle in accordance with the claim is a verification from Allah for that claimant, and everyone whom Allah verifies is truthful.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage presents the logical proof for the third premise in the argument for the truthfulness of a prophet. The author argues that when a miracle occurs after a claim of prophethood, it must be an act of Allah, and since Allah is truthful, He would only support a truthful claimant. The proof is illustrated with an analogy: if a king's messenger requests a sign and the king performs it, the people know the king confirms the messenger. Similarly, when the Prophet Muhammad asked Allah to split the moon and it happened, everyone knew that Allah was confirming his truthfulness. Therefore, the miracle serves as divine verification, and anyone so verified is truthful.

Key Terms
معجزة (miracle)
تصديق (verification)
دعوى (claim)
الملك العظيم (the great king)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof is circular: it assumes the miracle is from God and that God only supports truth.
Correction: The proof is not circular; it relies on the necessary knowledge that God, being perfect, would not support a liar. The miracle itself is taken as a direct act of God, and its purpose is inferred from context (following a claim).

Checkpoint
What analogy does al-Razi use to explain how a miracle proves a prophet's truthfulness?
A) A king verifying his messenger
B) A doctor healing a patient
C) A teacher testing a student
D) A merchant displaying goods

Key Takeaway
A miracle following a claim of prophethood is divine verification, proving the claimant's truthfulness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that the splitting of the moon was a divine verification of Muhammad's prophethood? If so, why does your life not reflect the certainty that would come from such knowledge? If not, what is holding you back from accepting it?
?
Imagine you were present when the Prophet made his claim and then the moon split. Would you have immediately believed, or would you have rationalized it away? What does your answer reveal about the state of your heart?
?
The analogy of the king shows that a true king would never verify a liar. If you claim to believe that Allah is the King of kings, how do you explain your occasional doubts about the truthfulness of His messengers? Where do those doubts come from, and what are you going to do about them starting today?

The First Objection: Miracles Lead to Skepticism
Al-Razi presents the first objection: the impossibility of miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first objection to the miracle-based proof of prophethood: that allowing miracles leads to logical absurdity and skepticism.

Core Idea
If miracles are possible, nothing is certain.

Al-Razi begins by presenting the most radical objection: miracles are impossible because they would undermine all certainty. This objection denies the very foundation of supernatural events.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. The passage presents the first objection in a logical sequence.
Notice the examples given to illustrate absurdity.
2
Trace the argument
Identify the steps: (1) premise: miracle requires break of custom; (2) denial: break is impossible; (3) proof: if allowed, leads to absurdity; (4) conclusion: impossible.
3
Reflect on the term 'sophistry'
Consider why the opponent claims that allowing miracles leads to sophistry. How does it affect certainty?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : الاعتراض على هذه الدلالة من وجوه :
الاعتراض الأول : أن قول القائل : إنه ظهر على يد المدعي للرسالة فعل خارق للعادة، هذا الكلام إنما يصح لو كان انخراق العادات جائزا ، ونحن نمنع هذا الجواز، والدليل على أنه ممتنع من أن تجويزه يفضي على السفسطة : أنا لو فتحنا هذا الباب لم نأمن أن تنقلب الجبال ذهبا إبريزاً، وأن ينقلب ماء البحر دما صرفا، وأن يكون هذا الشخص الذي نشاهده الآن شيخًا صار هرماً ، وأن يكون قد حدث هذه في الساعة شيخ من غير أب ولا أم ، ولكنا إذا شاهدنا زيدا لم نأمن من أن يكون الله خلق في هذه الساعة شيخًا من غير أب ولا أم مثل "زيد" في صورته وشكله وتخطيطه، ومعلوم أن تجويزه هذه الأشياء يفضي على الجهالات، ولما كان ذلك باطلا علمنا أن انخراق العادات غير ممكن.
الاعتراض الثاني: سلمنا أن انخراق العادات غير ممتنع إلا أنا نقول : لم قلتم : إن هذا حصل بإيجاد الله وتقرير هذا السؤال من وجوه :
الأول: نحن بين أمرين إما أن نثبت النفس الناطقة البشرية، وإما أنا لا نثبتها فإن أثبتنا النفس الناطقة، فلم لا يجوز أن يقا إن نفس النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مخالفة لسائر النفوس بالماهية والحقيقة، فهي لماهيتها المخصوصة وحقيقتها التي باعتبارها امتازت عن سائر الحقائق، قدرت على ما لا يقدر عليه غيره، وأما إن قلنا : إن القول بالنفوس الناطقة باطل، فلا بد أن نعترف أن لكل واحد من أشخاص الناس مزاجا مخصوصا وتركيبا ،مخصوصاً به امتاز عن سائر الأشخاص، فلم لا يجوز أن يقال: به امتاز هذا الشخص عن سائر الأشخاص علة لكونه قادرًا على الأفعال التي يعجز عنها غيره؟ ألا ترى أن لكل إنسان مزاجًا مخصوصا، وذلك المزاج يقتضي في ظاهره خلقاً، وفي باطنه خلقا لا يحصلان البتة في غيره، فلم لا يجوز أن يقال: تلك الخصوصية تكون مبدأ لتلك القدرة المخصوصة ؟ وعلى هذا التقدير لا يمكننا أن نعلم أن هذه المعجز هو فعل الله تعالى.
الوجه الثاني : في تقرير هذا المقام هب أن تلك المعجزات لم تحصل لأجل خصوصية نفسه أو خصوصية بدنه، لكن لا شك أن أنواع الأدوية كثيرة، والآثار الصادرة عنها عجيبة كثيرة، فلم لا يجوز أن يقال: إن هذا المدعى وجد دواء له قوة وخاصية تقتضي ظهور تلك الآثار والمعجزات عند تناول ذلك الدواء ؟ ألا ترى أن الناس يقولون : إن أكل الدواء الفلاني يزيد في الذكاء، وأكل الدواء الآخر يزيد في القوة الفلانية، فلم لا يجوز وجود دواء آخر يزيد في قوة الإدراك والعقل زيادة منتهية إلى حد هذا الاحتمال لا يمكن القطع بأن هذا المعجز فعل الله تعالى؟
الوجه الثالث : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : ظهور هذه المعجزات إنما كان بإعانة الجن والشياطين، وذلك لأنا وإن كنا نعرف مقادير عقول البشر، وقدرهم، إلا أنا لا نعرف مقادير عقول الشياطين وقدرهم فلعل هذه المعجزات حصلت بإعانة الشياطين، الإعجاز، ومع
If it is said: The objection to this indication is in several ways:
The first objection: That the statement of the one who says: 'A supernormal act appeared at the hand of the claimant of prophethood' – this statement is only valid if the breaking of customs is possible, and we deny this possibility. The proof that it is impossible is that allowing it leads to sophistry: if we open this door, we cannot be sure that mountains might turn into pure gold, that seawater might turn into pure blood, that this person we now see might become an old man, and that a sheikh might come into existence at this moment without father or mother, and if we see Zayd we cannot be sure that Allah did not create at this moment a sheikh without father or mother resembling Zayd in his image, form, and constitution. And it is known that allowing these things leads to absurdities. Since that is false, we know that the breaking of customs is impossible.
The second objection: We concede that breaking customs is not impossible, but we say: Why do you claim that this occurred by Allah's creation? The elaboration of this question has several aspects:
The first aspect: We are between two matters: either we affirm the rational human soul, or we do not affirm it. If we affirm the rational soul, why is it not permissible that it be said that the soul of the Prophet (PBUH) is different from other souls in essence and reality, so that due to its particular essence and reality by which it is distinguished from other realities, it is capable of what others cannot? And if we say that the claim of rational souls is false, then we must admit that each individual human has a particular temperament and composition by which he is distinguished from other individuals. So why is it not permissible that it be said: by that he is distinguished from other individuals as a cause for his being capable of actions that others cannot? Do you not see that every human has a particular temperament, and that temperament necessitates, in its appearance, a character, and in its interior, a character that are never found in another. So why is it not permissible that it be said: that particularity is the origin of that particular ability? On this estimate, we cannot know that this miracle is an act of Allah.
The second aspect: In elaboration of this point: suppose that those miracles did not occur due to the particularity of his soul or the particularity of his body. But there is no doubt that types of medicines are many, and their effects are wondrous and many. So why is it not permissible that it be said: this claimant found a medicine with a power and property necessitating the appearance of those effects and miracles when that medicine is taken? Do you not see that people say: consuming such-and-such a medicine increases intelligence, and consuming another medicine increases such-and-such ability? So why is it not permissible that there exists another medicine that increases the power of perception and intellect to an extreme degree such that this probability makes it impossible to be certain that this miracle is an act of Allah?
The third aspect: Why is it not permissible that it be said: the appearance of these miracles was only by the assistance of jinn and devils? This is because, although we know the extent of human intellects and abilities, we do not know the extent of the intellects of devils and their abilities. Perhaps these miracles occurred by the assistance of devils, the miraculous, and with...
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage presents three objections to the proof that a miracle following a claim of prophethood verifies the claimant's truthfulness. The first objection denies the possibility of miracles (breaking of natural laws) entirely, arguing that allowing such breaks leads to skepticism about all ordinary events and thus is absurd. The second objection concedes the possibility but questions whether the miracle must come from God, suggesting alternative causes: (a) the prophet's own soul or body may have unique powers due to its essence or temperament; (b) a special medicine could produce such effects; (c) jinn or devils might assist. The third objection is incomplete but proposes that jinn or devils could cause miracles. These objections typically set up the author's subsequent refutations.

Key Terms
انخراق العادات (breaking of customs)
السفسطة (sophistry)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: This objection reflects Al-Razi's own position.
Correction: Al-Razi presents this as an objection to be refuted later; it is not his view.

Checkpoint
What does the first objection claim would happen if we allow miracles (breaking of customs)?
A) Faith would be strengthened.
B) It would lead to sophistry and uncertainty.
C) Prophethood would be proven.
D) Nothing would change.

Key Takeaway
The first objection denies miracles because they would undermine all certainty and lead to absurdity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the objection that miracles would make the world unpredictable, do you ever feel a subtle doubt about the miracles of the prophets? How can you use the fact that this is an objection (not the truth) to strengthen your conviction?
?
The opponent argues that if we accept one miracle, we cannot be certain of anything, even seeing a person like Zayd. Do you live as if God could intervene at any moment, or do you rely on a closed system of cause and effect? What would change in your daily trust if you truly believed that Allah can break customs for His messengers?
?
Read the part about the absurd examples. Do you sometimes use similar reasoning to dismiss the possibility of divine intervention in your own life? What does this passage reveal about the danger of letting human logic limit your belief in Allah's power?

The Second Objection: Miracles May Have Natural Causes
Al-Razi presents the second objection: alternative natural causes for miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second objection: even if miracles are possible, they need not be from God; they could arise from the prophet's soul, temperament, medicine, or jinn assistance.

Core Idea
Miracles can be explained without God.

The second objection concedes the possibility of miracles but questions whether they must be divine. The opponent proposes alternative explanations: the prophet's unique soul, his bodily temperament, the effect of special medicines, or the assistance of jinn and devils.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
The passage presents three sub-aspects of the second objection. Read the Arabic and translation.
2
Identify the three sub-aspects
List the three alternative explanations: (1) rational soul, (2) medicine, (3) jinn and devils.
3
Consider the reasoning
For each sub-aspect, understand why the opponent thinks it is possible. How does each undermine the proof?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : الاعتراض على هذه الدلالة من وجوه :
الاعتراض الأول : أن قول القائل : إنه ظهر على يد المدعي للرسالة فعل خارق للعادة، هذا الكلام إنما يصح لو كان انخراق العادات جائزا ، ونحن نمنع هذا الجواز، والدليل على أنه ممتنع من أن تجويزه يفضي على السفسطة : أنا لو فتحنا هذا الباب لم نأمن أن تنقلب الجبال ذهبا إبريزاً، وأن ينقلب ماء البحر دما صرفا، وأن يكون هذا الشخص الذي نشاهده الآن شيخًا صار هرماً ، وأن يكون قد حدث هذه في الساعة شيخ من غير أب ولا أم ، ولكنا إذا شاهدنا زيدا لم نأمن من أن يكون الله خلق في هذه الساعة شيخًا من غير أب ولا أم مثل "زيد" في صورته وشكله وتخطيطه، ومعلوم أن تجويزه هذه الأشياء يفضي على الجهالات، ولما كان ذلك باطلا علمنا أن انخراق العادات غير ممكن.
الاعتراض الثاني: سلمنا أن انخراق العادات غير ممتنع إلا أنا نقول : لم قلتم : إن هذا حصل بإيجاد الله وتقرير هذا السؤال من وجوه :
الأول: نحن بين أمرين إما أن نثبت النفس الناطقة البشرية، وإما أنا لا نثبتها فإن أثبتنا النفس الناطقة، فلم لا يجوز أن يقا إن نفس النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مخالفة لسائر النفوس بالماهية والحقيقة، فهي لماهيتها المخصوصة وحقيقتها التي باعتبارها امتازت عن سائر الحقائق، قدرت على ما لا يقدر عليه غيره، وأما إن قلنا : إن القول بالنفوس الناطقة باطل، فلا بد أن نعترف أن لكل واحد من أشخاص الناس مزاجا مخصوصا وتركيبا ،مخصوصاً به امتاز عن سائر الأشخاص، فلم لا يجوز أن يقال: به امتاز هذا الشخص عن سائر الأشخاص علة لكونه قادرًا على الأفعال التي يعجز عنها غيره؟ ألا ترى أن لكل إنسان مزاجًا مخصوصا، وذلك المزاج يقتضي في ظاهره خلقاً، وفي باطنه خلقا لا يحصلان البتة في غيره، فلم لا يجوز أن يقال: تلك الخصوصية تكون مبدأ لتلك القدرة المخصوصة ؟ وعلى هذا التقدير لا يمكننا أن نعلم أن هذه المعجز هو فعل الله تعالى.
الوجه الثاني : في تقرير هذا المقام هب أن تلك المعجزات لم تحصل لأجل خصوصية نفسه أو خصوصية بدنه، لكن لا شك أن أنواع الأدوية كثيرة، والآثار الصادرة عنها عجيبة كثيرة، فلم لا يجوز أن يقال: إن هذا المدعى وجد دواء له قوة وخاصية تقتضي ظهور تلك الآثار والمعجزات عند تناول ذلك الدواء ؟ ألا ترى أن الناس يقولون : إن أكل الدواء الفلاني يزيد في الذكاء، وأكل الدواء الآخر يزيد في القوة الفلانية، فلم لا يجوز وجود دواء آخر يزيد في قوة الإدراك والعقل زيادة منتهية إلى حد هذا الاحتمال لا يمكن القطع بأن هذا المعجز فعل الله تعالى؟
الوجه الثالث : لم لا يجوز أن يقال : ظهور هذه المعجزات إنما كان بإعانة الجن والشياطين، وذلك لأنا وإن كنا نعرف مقادير عقول البشر، وقدرهم، إلا أنا لا نعرف مقادير عقول الشياطين وقدرهم فلعل هذه المعجزات حصلت بإعانة الشياطين، الإعجاز، ومع
If it is said: The objection to this indication is in several ways:
The first objection: That the statement of the one who says: 'A supernormal act appeared at the hand of the claimant of prophethood' – this statement is only valid if the breaking of customs is possible, and we deny this possibility. The proof that it is impossible is that allowing it leads to sophistry: if we open this door, we cannot be sure that mountains might turn into pure gold, that seawater might turn into pure blood, that this person we now see might become an old man, and that a sheikh might come into existence at this moment without father or mother, and if we see Zayd we cannot be sure that Allah did not create at this moment a sheikh without father or mother resembling Zayd in his image, form, and constitution. And it is known that allowing these things leads to absurdities. Since that is false, we know that the breaking of customs is impossible.
The second objection: We concede that breaking customs is not impossible, but we say: Why do you claim that this occurred by Allah's creation? The elaboration of this question has several aspects:
The first aspect: We are between two matters: either we affirm the rational human soul, or we do not affirm it. If we affirm the rational soul, why is it not permissible that it be said that the soul of the Prophet (PBUH) is different from other souls in essence and reality, so that due to its particular essence and reality by which it is distinguished from other realities, it is capable of what others cannot? And if we say that the claim of rational souls is false, then we must admit that each individual human has a particular temperament and composition by which he is distinguished from other individuals. So why is it not permissible that it be said: by that he is distinguished from other individuals as a cause for his being capable of actions that others cannot? Do you not see that every human has a particular temperament, and that temperament necessitates, in its appearance, a character, and in its interior, a character that are never found in another. So why is it not permissible that it be said: that particularity is the origin of that particular ability? On this estimate, we cannot know that this miracle is an act of Allah.
The second aspect: In elaboration of this point: suppose that those miracles did not occur due to the particularity of his soul or the particularity of his body. But there is no doubt that types of medicines are many, and their effects are wondrous and many. So why is it not permissible that it be said: this claimant found a medicine with a power and property necessitating the appearance of those effects and miracles when that medicine is taken? Do you not see that people say: consuming such-and-such a medicine increases intelligence, and consuming another medicine increases such-and-such ability? So why is it not permissible that there exists another medicine that increases the power of perception and intellect to an extreme degree such that this probability makes it impossible to be certain that this miracle is an act of Allah?
The third aspect: Why is it not permissible that it be said: the appearance of these miracles was only by the assistance of jinn and devils? This is because, although we know the extent of human intellects and abilities, we do not know the extent of the intellects of devils and their abilities. Perhaps these miracles occurred by the assistance of devils, the miraculous, and with...
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage presents three objections to the proof that a miracle following a claim of prophethood verifies the claimant's truthfulness. The first objection denies the possibility of miracles (breaking of natural laws) entirely, arguing that allowing such breaks leads to skepticism about all ordinary events and thus is absurd. The second objection concedes the possibility but questions whether the miracle must come from God, suggesting alternative causes: (a) the prophet's own soul or body may have unique powers due to its essence or temperament; (b) a special medicine could produce such effects; (c) jinn or devils might assist. The third objection is incomplete but proposes that jinn or devils could cause miracles. These objections typically set up the author's subsequent refutations.

Key Terms
النفس الناطقة (rational soul)
المزاج (temperament)
الأدوية (medicines)
الجن (jinn)
الشياطين (devils)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: These alternatives are plausible and undermine the proof entirely.
Correction: The objection raises possibilities, but Al-Razi will later refute them; they are not accepted as valid.

Checkpoint
According to the second objection, which of the following is NOT proposed as an alternative explanation for miracles?
A) The prophet's unique soul
B) The prophet's unique temperament
C) A special medicine
D) The prophet's own divine nature

Key Takeaway
The second objection argues that even if miracles occur, they could have natural or created rather than divine causes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness something extraordinary in your life, do you instinctively search for a natural explanation to avoid admitting Allah's direct involvement? What does that reveal about your heart's state? Confront this tendency and ask yourself how you would react if you were certain it was from Allah.
?
Imagine the Prophet Muhammad's miracles were actually from his own soul or a medicine—would that change your faith? Why does the source of a miracle matter for your relationship with Allah? Be honest: do you rely on signs to strengthen your belief, or is your faith rooted in something deeper?
?
You have just read three alternative explanations for miracles. Which one tempts you most as a way to avoid submitting to Allah's power? Pray to Allah to purify your heart from seeking excuses to evade His signs, and commit to accepting His miracles as His direct action.
